  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a4c7b141-766c-430a-bd49-1e26f016bf1f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer6712761783749277012">Paula es el libro más conmovedor, más personal y más íntimo de Isabel Allende. Junto al lecho en que agonizaba su hija Paula, la gran narradora chilena escribió la historia de su familia y de sí misma con el propósito de regalársela a Paula cuando ésta superara el dramático trance. El resultado se convirtió en un autorretrato de insólita emotividad y en una exquisita recre</span>
  <span id="freeText6712761783749277012" style="display:none">Paula es el libro más conmovedor, más personal y más íntimo de Isabel Allende. Junto al lecho en que agonizaba su hija Paula, la gran narradora chilena escribió la historia de su familia y de sí misma con el propósito de regalársela a Paula cuando ésta superara el dramático trance. El resultado se convirtió en un autorretrato de insólita emotividad y en una exquisita recreación de la sensibilidad de las mujeres de nuestra época.</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I've read it twice and each time it made me very angry. She knew her daughter suffered from a hereditary, little understood disorder, and yet when Pau<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I've read it twice and each time it made me very angry. She knew her daughter suffered from a hereditary, little understood disorder, and yet when Paula says she feels unwell, her mother puts it down to her whiny nature and ignores it until it's too late. To me, the final dream-sequence scene with the slippers seemed like an attempt at an apology, but it didn't work. I gave up on Allende after The Infinite Plan, the book released after this one.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1593237821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593237821" />
    <a title="Brina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2933855-brina"><img alt="Brina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601675085p2/2933855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1593237821?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brina" href="/user/show/2933855-brina">Brina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060172534" href="/book/show/76626.Paula">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=isabel-allende">isabel-allende</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=hispanic-culture">hispanic-culture</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593237821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14960510915820759772">Isabel Allende has long been my favorite author since I read her House of the Spirits for the first time nearly twenty years ago. Since then, I have reread her opus three times, as well as a number of her novels and memoir The Sum of Our Days. Until now, however, I had been avoiding her first memoir Paula, which details the year and a half of her life where she dealt with her daughter's long illness that eventually lead to her death. Needing a book from the 1990s for my women's 20th century chal</span>
  <span id="freeText14960510915820759772" style="display:none">Isabel Allende has long been my favorite author since I read her House of the Spirits for the first time nearly twenty years ago. Since then, I have reread her opus three times, as well as a number of her novels and memoir The Sum of Our Days. Until now, however, I had been avoiding her first memoir Paula, which details the year and a half of her life where she dealt with her daughter's long illness that eventually lead to her death. Needing a book from the 1990s for my women's 20th century challenge, I decided to grapple with Paula. What awaited me was a heart rending account of Allende's in which she details her life up until she started her long goodbye to her daughter. <br /><br />After I read The Sum of Our Days, I was left feeling as though I knew Allende well enough to be a friend or relative. She has a way of relating herself that one feels like they are sharing a cup of coffee with her and reminiscing. If I felt the connection after this memoir, I felt like a close friend of hers following Paula. Allende was born in Peru in 1942 as her parents were serving as diplomats in Lima. Following the birth of her two brothers, her father Tomas abandoned the family, and Allende's mother retreated with her three young children to Santiago, Chile, the city they had inhabited since the time of the conquistadors. It is this city that Allende refers to as home and is the setting of her first three novels and short story collection. At the time of this publication while she was grappling with Paula's illness, Allende was unsure if she would ever write fiction again, although, when she resumed, Santiago possessed a magnetic pull and would play a role in most subsequent work. <br /><br />Paula unfortunately inherited a disorder called porphyria from her father. At age twenty eight after only being married for one year, she experienced complications from the disease and slipped into a coma in a Madrid hospital. Her mother and husband rarely left her side for the next six months as doctors repeatedly tested her to see if they could find a break through. Isabel could not write, her sole focus being that Paula should get well, and her agent urged her to write Paula a letter. Isabel decided to tell Paula the story of their family history, even if she would never experience these memories for herself again. It was in this regard that Allende rediscovered her writing voice despite the tragedies befalling her family. <br /><br />Allende alternated telling her family's story with the present situation of Paula's illness. We learn about Allende's grandparents, the real life inspiration for Esteban and Clara Trueba in House of the Spirits. Allende inherited Clara's propensity to communicate with spirits and shared a special relationship with Paula as she lingered between death and life. Later she tells us how the overthrow of her uncle Salvador Allende's government lead the family to seek asylum in Venezuela. It was in Caracas that Allende became a published novelist and lead her to both fame and a new life in the United States as she reached middle age. Yet, just as Allende made a name for herself, Paula fell ill. No one should have to bury their children, but Allende put her career on hold so that her daughter would not suffer during the end of her life. This book is as much of a letter to Paula as it is to preserve her memories. <br /><br />I have read a good many of Allende's books at this point. I have experienced a fictionalized version of her family history, but none of her story telling prepared me for this true heart breaking tale. I have always enjoyed curling up with Allende's books at any time of the year and still consider her my favorite fiction author. Yet seeing how she faced her daughter's illness and eventually recovered to continue her career shows me that Isabel Allende is just as an amazing person. I hope that she should not have to experience heart break like this again, and that she should continue writing for the rest of her days. As House of the Spirits remains my favorite book of the them all, Paul ranks 4.75 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14960510915820759772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8955487623217714444">What could be more complicated than watching our daughter die? The insane hope of recovery than the long accompaniment until the end?<br/><br/>"Paula" therefore begins with a letter from Isabel Allende to her sick daughter. She tells him the story of her family, a saga full of legends and imagination. Still, this narrative of the past is interrupted by the events of the present, the deterioration of Paula's health, the distress, the treatments and the superstitions that try to overcome the evil and even t</span>
  <span id="freeText8955487623217714444" style="display:none">What could be more complicated than watching our daughter die? The insane hope of recovery than the long accompaniment until the end?<br /><br />"Paula" therefore begins with a letter from Isabel Allende to her sick daughter. She tells him the story of her family, a saga full of legends and imagination. Still, this narrative of the past is interrupted by the events of the present, the deterioration of Paula's health, the distress, the treatments and the superstitions that try to overcome the evil and even the intense moments when one wonders if it would not be better to shorten his sufferings.<br /><br />Two parallel wefts thus are woven, and the story of the family becomes that of Isabel. She loves her work and also the history of Chile. The demanding hours of the coup, the death of her uncle Salvator Allende, the military regime with its kidnappings and tortures. The idea of ​​a letter to her daughter has disappeared; there is only writing as a survival meaning, an outlet for the painful emotions of a loved one's agony.<br /><br />Isabel Allende tells herself without shame. I even wonder how all the people she mentions could have received these indiscreet descriptions.<br /><br />A touching testimony on pain of losing a child. On the life of a woman with a unique destiny in the tumults and landscapes of South America.</span>

<div id="review_67543116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67543116" />
    <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely"><img alt="K.D. Absolutely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471967140p2/2156200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67543116?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.D. Absolutely" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060927219" href="/book/show/234050.Paula">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jinky</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      501 Must Read Books
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=501">501</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67543116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14134127966557270645"><b>
  <i>"What do you want us to learn, Paula?</i>
</b><br/><br/>After reading up to her closing lines: <i>Godspeed, Paula, woman. Welcome, Paula, spirit</i> on page 330 of this amazing 1995-published memoir, still the question above is the one that reverberates inside my head. This is one of the questions the 49-y/o Chilean-American novelist, <b>Isabel Allende</b> asked her 29-y/o comatose daughter, <b>Paula Frias Allende</b>.<br/><br/>The reason is <b>Bhang</b>. My 29-y/o officemate who is currently comatose right after giving birth to a healthy baby boy</span>
  <span id="freeText14134127966557270645" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"What do you want us to learn, Paula?</i>
</b><br /><br />After reading up to her closing lines: <i>Godspeed, Paula, woman. Welcome, Paula, spirit</i> on page 330 of this amazing 1995-published memoir, still the question above is the one that reverberates inside my head. This is one of the questions the 49-y/o Chilean-American novelist, <b>Isabel Allende</b> asked her 29-y/o comatose daughter, <b>Paula Frias Allende</b>.<br /><br />The reason is <b>Bhang</b>. My 29-y/o officemate who is currently comatose right after giving birth to a healthy baby boy (her second) last month. She had a stroke due to lack of oxygen while giving birth and now has to be fed like a baby. Although she can open her eyes, she does not recognize anyone. We already passed the envelope. We formed a 24-hr prayer brigade and I have my slot and dutifully do my share of uttering prayers for her everyday. However, just like Isabel's question to her 29-y/o daughter, Paula Frias Allende, there must be a reason why Bhang is in coma. There could be something else that we, her officemates, can do for her and learn something from this.<br /><br />Bhang and I are not close. In fact, we never said a word to each other since she joined the company in 2005. Maybe it is because our desks are in the different floors. Maybe because our wide age difference. Maybe she is in Marketing and I am in IT and her group does not use the system I am maintaining. Maybe we are not destined to be friends or did not have a chance to bump into each other and introduce ourselves. <br /><br />The sad news of what happened to her came out on the same day I celebrated my 46th birthday last month. The attendees of my party, passed on the envelope and I even considered the party contest's humble prizes should be cut down and give instead to Bhang. The week later, I sent an email for us to form a prayer brigade which is still in-place even up to now.<br /><br />Last week, Bhang already left the hospital. She is still comatose but her relatives decide to just take care of her at home. Same as what happened in the book: Isabel decided to take care of her daughter Paula at home because she thought that the familiar surroundings was something that could help Paula to recover. Maybe it is the same reason why Bhang's family decided to bring her home.<br /><br />I told my wife about Bhang and when I updated her a couple of days back, she said give more help. I told her that Bhang and I are not that close. She said as a mother, she feels sad not only for Bhang but also for the newborn baby. With his mother in coma, who is now taking care of him. I guess her mother's heart is speaking to my wife. Give more money to Bhang, she said.<br /><br />So, this month-end, we we will have <i>Pancit for Bhang</i> in the office. The idea of cooking noodles is based on what my wife's officemates they did, last year, for their very sick officemate: <i>Lugaw Para Kay XXXXX</i>. Somebody cooked a big bowl of rice porridge and sold a small bowl at exorbitant price. All proceeds went to the family of the very sick man.<br /><br />This may not be a proper review for an amazing book <i>Paula</i> by <b>Isabel Allende</b> of novels like <i>The House of Spirits, Love and Shadows, Eva Luna, The Infinite Plan,</i> etc. However, the fact that it made me think of what else should be done for Bhang means that this is a powerful book. Paula and Bhang. The same age. Young women. Talented, a whole stretch of bright future ahead of them. What do their experiences want to teach us?<br /><br />There must still be something we can do. There must be.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14134127966557270645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060172534" href="/book/show/76626.Paula">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6700518-lorna?shelf=biography">biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6700518-lorna?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6700518-lorna?shelf=signed-by-author">signed-by-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6700518-lorna?shelf=latin-america">latin-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6700518-lorna?shelf=california">california</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227189038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3794655325383948969"><i>Paula</i> by Isabel Allende is an autobiographical account of her family's experiences in Chile, writing feverishly at the bedside of her daughter, Paula, as she lay in a coma from a genetic neurological disease in Barcelona, Spain. At first it was written for Paula so that she will not be lost or afraid when she awoke; then as it became clearer that this wouldn't happen, Allende continued to write as a cathartic of the time her family was driven from their home in Chile following the military coup </span>
  <span id="freeText3794655325383948969" style="display:none"><i>Paula</i> by Isabel Allende is an autobiographical account of her family's experiences in Chile, writing feverishly at the bedside of her daughter, Paula, as she lay in a coma from a genetic neurological disease in Barcelona, Spain. At first it was written for Paula so that she will not be lost or afraid when she awoke; then as it became clearer that this wouldn't happen, Allende continued to write as a cathartic of the time her family was driven from their home in Chile following the military coup of 1973 and the assassination of her uncle, Salvatore Allende. She speaks to life in her beloved Chile during the tyrannical regime of Augusto Pinochet. She recounts the time her beloved grandfather was dying. Unable to return to Chile, she began writing him a letter but as she continued to write, Allende announced to her family that she had written a book. This became a bestseller in Latin America, and soon, around the world, <i>The House of Spirits.</i> Woven throughout the book <i>Paula</i>, Isabel Allende writes of Paula, the beautiful child that she was, and the courageous and giving adult that she became. It is very much a process of the stages of grief and letting go of someone that we love, as she embraces Paula's new husband and the process where together they realize that they must let Paula go. This was a beautiful and loving tribute, not only to Paula, but to Isabel Allende.<br /><br />On a personal note, visiting Latin America in 1981, I became very drawn to the politics and literature of that time, particularly in Colombia, Chile and Argentina. It was hard to forget the beautiful city of Santiago, as we all gazed upon the Palace of Governors and were told that this is where Salvatore Allende "committed suicide." Or during our stay in Buenos Aires, looking down from my hotel window and seeing women marching in the park below, all dressed in black, including lace mantillas, and carrying signs with the names of family members who had disappeared. This was the weekly march of the mothers of the disappeared, the <i>desaparecidos.</i> Lastly, having had the pleasure and honor of attending some book signings by Isabel Allende, she always signs her books with a flower. It is in this book, she relates as the dictatorship of Pinochet was becoming more oppressive, she accepted many of the external signs of the Flower Children, <i>"adopting flowers in her clothing, painting them on the walls of their home and car--enormous yellow sunflowers and bright dahlias. . . "</i><br /><br /><i>I am Chilean, I come from a 'long petal of sea and wine and snow,' as Pablo Neruda described my country, and you're from there, too, Paula, even though you bear the indelible stamp of the Caribbean where you spent the years of your childhood."<br /><br />"In Chile, we are influenced by the eternal presence of the mountains that separate us from the rest of the continent, and by a sense of precariousness inevitable in a region of geological and political catastrophes. Everything trembles beneath our feet; we know no security."<br /><br />" I was transported with implacable clarity to the times I lived in Chile under the heavy mantle of terror: censorship and self-censorship, denunciations, curfew, soldiers with faces camouflaged . . . arrests in the street, homes, offices. . . .helping fugitives find asylum, sleepless nights when we had someone hidden in our home, clumsy schemes to slip information out of the country."<br /><br />"It came to me how for countless centuries women have lost their children, how it is humanity's most ancient and inevitable sorrow. I am not alone, most mothers know this pain, it breaks their heart but they go on living because they must protect and love those who are left."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3794655325383948969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1090023276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090023276" />
    <a title="Book Concierge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge"><img alt="Book Concierge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324904606p2/1628041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1090023276?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Book Concierge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Book Concierge" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge">Book Concierge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060927219" href="/book/show/234050.Paula">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=concierge">concierge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=strong-women">strong-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=literature">literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=women-writers">women-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=politics">politics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1090023276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11512810303417052661">When Isabel Allende’s daughter became gravely ill and fell into a coma, the author spent days at Paula’s bedside. At her own mother’s urging, Allende began to write the story of her family for Paula in an attempt to connect her child with her ancestors, <i>“…so that when you wake up you will not feel so lost.” </i><br/><br/>Evocative, heart-rending, luminous, suspenseful, triumphant – I cannot think of enough adjectives to describe this beautifully written memoir. Allende lays her soul bare on the page. She brin</span>
  <span id="freeText11512810303417052661" style="display:none">When Isabel Allende’s daughter became gravely ill and fell into a coma, the author spent days at Paula’s bedside. At her own mother’s urging, Allende began to write the story of her family for Paula in an attempt to connect her child with her ancestors, <i>“…so that when you wake up you will not feel so lost.” </i><br /><br />Evocative, heart-rending, luminous, suspenseful, triumphant – I cannot think of enough adjectives to describe this beautifully written memoir. Allende lays her soul bare on the page. She brings her own grandparents, uncles, cousins, parents, brothers, friends to life as she attempts to reach the comatose Paula. Her family connections are full of world-famous people – not the least of which was her uncle Salvador Allende – and she had a rather privileged upbringing. She traveled extensively with her mother and stepfather, who was a diplomat, and attended private schools. But all her advantages could not protect Allende from life’s setbacks and tragedies. <br /><br />With unfailing honesty she relates everything – from being sexually molested as a child to being a television star, from a sheltered young woman to a feminist and political exile, from a traditional wife and mother to a reckless love affair with an Argentinian trumpeter. She also includes many examples of her deep connections to the mystical and spiritual; it’s easy to see why she writes magical realism so well.<br /><br />The work moves back and forth from Allende’s history to the events in Paula’s hospital room. Those scenes at her daughter’s bedside were some of the most emotional. The fierceness with which Allende fought to bring her precious child back from the abyss, the refusal to take “No” for an answer, the determination to bring her daughter back to California and her home overlooking San Francisco Bay – these passages in the book reveal the woman today, while the scenes relating her history show how she came to be this strong woman. <br /><br />It took me a while to get into the book. The writing is very dense; a paragraph can last three pages. But once I got used to the rhythm of her writing I was totally immersed and engaged. Allende’s gift for storytelling is evident. There were passages that evoked laughter, sections where I recognized my own relationships with my brothers or grandparents, and scenes that had me in tears or gasping aloud. Towards the end of the book she writes this:<br /><i>I try to remember who I was once but I find only disguises, masks, projections, the confused images of a woman I can’t recognize. Am I the feminist I thought I was, or the frivolous girl who appeared on television wearing nothing but ostrich feathers? The obsessive mother, the unfaithful wife, the fearless adventurer, or the cowardly woman? Am I the person who helped political fugitives find asylum or the one who ran away because she couldn’t handle fear?</i><br />The answer, of course, is that she is all these women. Her experiences may be unique, but her reactions are universal. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11512810303417052661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This is a story of hope and happiness, brought to the surface of a white page as the last letter of a grieving mother to her daughter. <br/><br/>It's also the story of Allende's days as she starts writing, as she survives poverty in a foreign country, as she finds the love of her life.   <span id="freeText14145445092024395989" style="display:none">The heartbreaking and heartwarming recount of the days (and years) that preceded the death of Paula, Isabel Allende's daughter. This is a story of hope and happiness, brought to the surface of a white page as the last letter of a grieving mother to her daughter. <br /><br />It's also the story of Allende's days as she starts writing, as she survives poverty in a foreign country, as she finds the love of her life. It's an ode to perseverance, to love, to surviving and thriving even through the hardest tragedies. And it's full of humor and laughs, because, like the life it reflects, this story has a bit of everything and that is what makes it so great.<br /><br />I do recommend this book, but beware, you may need some time to recover after reading it.</span>

  <span id="freeText14257223492875768829" style="display:none">well written, but so tedious! i just can't get into this book. by no means am i belittling the very sad situation with her daughter, paula. since the author wants to express her spiritual gifts and insights, here's mine: spirits know everything once they have passed over. all the secrets of family, of you, of history are revealed to them. they don't read novels.<br /><br />yeah, her childhood, etc, isn't the greatest and some crap things happen, but the family is part of the top-crust upper class. it couldn't have been that bad.<br /><br />i think i'd prefer a fictional novel, though i think that some of these stories must be slightly enhanced with imagination - don't we all do this to our childhood memories?<br /><br />it seems like she's just bragging about her family and her life, which i would care more about it if was my family, or my own mother's life. to make matters worse (and completely unrelated to the actual content of the "novel") the back of this very large book is just a photo of the author. no teaser, no reviews, just her photo. i get it, you love yourself. everyone should love themselves. but good god! you wrote a whole book about yourself! yay to you for being beautiful, too.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8252506510747326676">Several years ago I read Isabel Allende's fiction and remembered liking it, so enroute to the library checkout I grabbed her nonfiction book, "Paula," on impulse. I have mixed feelings about it. It is a definite page-turner, alternating between the true story of Allende's daughter Paula and her terrible health condition, and the flashbacks of Allende's own very eventful life. Allende wrote the personal history as a way of telling Paula her story and staying sane during the health ordeal. She is </span>
  <span id="freeText8252506510747326676" style="display:none">Several years ago I read Isabel Allende's fiction and remembered liking it, so enroute to the library checkout I grabbed her nonfiction book, "Paula," on impulse. I have mixed feelings about it. It is a definite page-turner, alternating between the true story of Allende's daughter Paula and her terrible health condition, and the flashbacks of Allende's own very eventful life. Allende wrote the personal history as a way of telling Paula her story and staying sane during the health ordeal. She is definitely a gifted storyteller, and her stories about Chile during the coup were fascinating, but she is not always a moral or likable narrator. I had to wonder how much poor Paula, if she ever emerged from the coma, would want to read about her mother's sex life. Allende proved a bit too self-centered and goddess-y for me, but overall I still enjoyed it. The book made me want to revisit her fiction again to see if I would like it as an older and wiser? woman. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8252506510747326676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12729067327972521899" style="display:none">What a wonderful epic story! An ode to life, to love, to the unique bond between mother and child. <br />I am so so sorry for the lost! It is hard even to imagine the hurt of a mother who accompanies his child to death. <br />I want to write about its beauty - but I am afraid I won't pay respect to a devastating hurt. <br />I've just "met" Allende in December, 2019 when I was reading "The House of Spirits". <div id="review_3740056" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3740056" />
    <a title="Bookshop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/233375-bookshop"><img alt="Bookshop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1185717120p2/233375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3740056?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookshop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookshop" href="/user/show/233375-bookshop">Bookshop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006548560" href="/book/show/837668.Paula">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3740056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14329024598793670375">Isabel Allende starts this book as a collection of letters to her daughter who fell into a coma. She wrote this while caring for her in a Madrid hospital so that when Paula, the daughter who might be suffering from brain damage, woke up, she could read everything about her ancestry.<br/><br/>Isabel Allende is known for her story-telling but I've actually never read her fiction. Sorry, I lied. I read Daughter of Fortune a long time ago but I've forgotten everything about it. But I like her biography, My In</span>
  <span id="freeText14329024598793670375" style="display:none">Isabel Allende starts this book as a collection of letters to her daughter who fell into a coma. She wrote this while caring for her in a Madrid hospital so that when Paula, the daughter who might be suffering from brain damage, woke up, she could read everything about her ancestry.<br /><br />Isabel Allende is known for her story-telling but I've actually never read her fiction. Sorry, I lied. I read Daughter of Fortune a long time ago but I've forgotten everything about it. But I like her biography, My Invented Country. I like her humorous and fluent writing which are occasionally peppered with scandalous or self-depreciating anecdotes.<br /><br />Because I read My Invented Country first, the first half of the book read like a repetition. I did not mind as it was really engaging. I was reduced to tears by Paula's husband's devotion to her. I laughed out loud reading the different antics Allende employed while she was with her grandfather. I scorned and judged her (not the daughter's) numerous love affairs.<br /><br />The second half of the book (there is actually no such physical distinction in the book) starts when Paula was moved from the hospital in Madrid to Allende's house in the US. Then, the manner of writing changes and the fun stops. There are a lot of psychicbabble, a lot of new-age optimism, a lot of universal-love talks. It bored me because they are used excessively. Even the moving emotions I felt earlier seem to disappear like plump juicy strawberry coated with cheap layer of caramel. It was rather nauseating.<br /><br />Anyway, from an extraordinary beginning, the book ends rather poorly. So I rate it a three. It's still a good, light read but, if you're looking for an honest account, this book doesn't quite convey it because, in the end, there was too much artificial glorification of all parties involved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14329024598793670375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_539211708" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/539211708" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11255849-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565547225p2/11255849.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/539211708?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/11255849-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061564901" href="/book/show/2335787.Paula">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=women-and-books">women-and-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=global-intrigue">global-intrigue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=latin-america">latin-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=war-stories">war-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer539211708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16975162359715391978">Isabel Allende wrote that her memoir was published despite reservations from her agents and some editors who felt that the topic, plus the fact that she had exposed herself to the "public gaze without holding anything back," could harm her. Thank goodness she went ahead with it.<br/><br/>Part of what makes this book so beautiful is the tone: she wrote it as a letter to her daughter who was lying in a coma in Madrid, Spain. Letter writing had been going on for years in this family. Isabel usually wrote a l</span>
  <span id="freeText16975162359715391978" style="display:none">Isabel Allende wrote that her memoir was published despite reservations from her agents and some editors who felt that the topic, plus the fact that she had exposed herself to the "public gaze without holding anything back," could harm her. Thank goodness she went ahead with it.<br /><br />Part of what makes this book so beautiful is the tone: she wrote it as a letter to her daughter who was lying in a coma in Madrid, Spain. Letter writing had been going on for years in this family. Isabel usually wrote a letter a day to her mother, who would respond daily and the two women would bundle up the letters with ribbons and store them in closets. Such is the bond between three generation of women in this family. <br /><br />Paula was a twenty-something newly wed, who had just returned from a spiritual retreat with nuns at a school where she helped underprivileged children, when she started to vomit and get feverish. She had had a condition called porphyria for several years, and it had worsened. Her mom, Isabel, also a novelist, was celebrating the launch of her book when her agent came running to tell her that her daughter had been hospitalized. As she sat by her side, she started to write this book.<br /><br />What's interesting about her account is how she intertwines the present action, with a historical narrative of her family--and this is one family that saw trials. Isabel Allende was the niece of the former executed president of Chile. Her parents (and later she and her family) had to escape to exile during the coup. Throughout her life, she lived in Chile, Bolivia, Lebanon, Spain, and Venezuela, so you get snippets of information and rich cultural history from South America (ah the beauty of memoirs). I also really liked Ernesto, her daughter's husband, and how she painstakingly described their love and relationship. Isabel doesn't hold back about her life either, giving some really intimate details to highlight character flaw. <br /><br />What I didn't care for was how Part I was a letter, and Part II was a bit telling because it switched from letter form directed to Paula, to exposition directed to the reader. Occasionally the factual elements paused the story a bit, but there was so much to learn about Chile, about exiles, about three generations of women, about this extraordinary family and the extraordinary woman lying on the bed...that it's certainly worth the read. <br /><br />A melancholic tale but a worthy one for sure. I will be adding Allende's fiction to my list. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16975162359715391978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10919366941368679743">Discussion Guide:<br/>(Questions compiled by Rihab Sebaaly)<br/><br/>1-	Paula is the first nonfiction book written by Allende. Did you notice this? Did you feel that Paula was written by someone with no experience in nonfiction books?<br/><br/>2-	Where Do you love Allende more: in nonfiction or in fiction books? And why?<br/><br/>3-	Allende rewrote Chile’s history and her own history in this book. Do you think she was objective especially when she narrated the events surrounding Salvador Allende's life and politics?<br/><br/>4-	Did you enj</span>
  <span id="freeText10919366941368679743" style="display:none">Discussion Guide:<br />(Questions compiled by Rihab Sebaaly)<br /><br />1-	Paula is the first nonfiction book written by Allende. Did you notice this? Did you feel that Paula was written by someone with no experience in nonfiction books?<br /><br />2-	Where Do you love Allende more: in nonfiction or in fiction books? And why?<br /><br />3-	Allende rewrote Chile’s history and her own history in this book. Do you think she was objective especially when she narrated the events surrounding Salvador Allende's life and politics?<br /><br />4-	Did you enjoy the parts where Allende described the political life in Chile? Where you interested ?<br /><br />5-	How did you find Allende’s relationship with her mother and her step-father? And how do you think the absence of her father could have influenced her personality?<br /><br />6-	Do you think Allende reacted to her daughter illness like any other woman would? Or did you find her more sensitive and less realistic?<br /><br />7-	Do you think it was selfish of Allende to hold on that hard to her daughter instead of letting her go?<br /><br />8-	Which was your favorite character and why?<br /><br />9-	Allende wanted to restore to her daughter the past she might have lost if she woke up. Do you think this book would have helped Paula after recovery? Or was this book a act of healing for Allende herself?<br /><br />10-	Would you hold on that hard to someone in the same conditions as Paula?<br /><br />11-	Did you like the way Allende wrote her memories? Did you find them vivid or boring?<br /><br />12-	Did you like how Allende went from her past to her present, i.e. the transitions between her memories and her daughter’s coma?<br /><br />13-	What did you find the most in this book: happiness or sadness? Hope or despair?<br /><br />14-	Did you finish this book wanting to read another book by Allende or not?<br /><br />15-	If you compare Paula’s husband love and her mother's love, do you think they both acted out of extreme love? Do you think Paula’s husband could have acted any differently?<br /><br />16-	Allende is a non-believer, do you think it would have been easier for her to overcome Paula’s sickness and death if she was a believer?<br /><br />17-	What do you think of death in general? And how do you personally react to illness?<br /><br /><br />Book Themes:<br /><br />1-	What do you think the main themes are in this book?<br /><br />2-	Do you think that this book reflects beautifully a mother's unconditional love? Or did you find some exaggeration in Allende's affection to her daughter?<br /><br />3-	Do you think this book fits to our main theme of “motherhood”?</span>

<div id="review_293227762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293227762" />
    <a title="Hoda Marmar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3655700-hoda-marmar"><img alt="Hoda Marmar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572216889p2/3655700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293227762?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hoda Marmar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hoda Marmar" href="/user/show/3655700-hoda-marmar">Hoda Marmar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655700-hoda-marmar?shelf=online-bookoholics">online-bookoholics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293227762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14253626497262803902">Maybe a 3.5 stars rating? Not sure.<br/>The idea behind this book is dramatic and beautiful: Isabel Allende's daughter Paula is sick, gets admitted to the hospital, slips into a coma and eventually dies. What would the storyteller and writer Isabel Allende do at her daughter's bedside for over a year? She would talk to her unconscious daughter, and would write her all the memories she has about her own life and family history to pass the cold waiting hours until Paula wakes up. That manuscript would </span>
  <span id="freeText14253626497262803902" style="display:none">Maybe a 3.5 stars rating? Not sure.<br />The idea behind this book is dramatic and beautiful: Isabel Allende's daughter Paula is sick, gets admitted to the hospital, slips into a coma and eventually dies. What would the storyteller and writer Isabel Allende do at her daughter's bedside for over a year? She would talk to her unconscious daughter, and would write her all the memories she has about her own life and family history to pass the cold waiting hours until Paula wakes up. That manuscript would fill all of the loops in her memory, she just needs to wake up.<br />We read this book as part of Bookoholics Book Club's online 2018 reading list which theme is Motherhood. This book is quite fitting. I really enjoyed lots of parts in it, especially the ones about Isabel's growing up as a kid around her grandma, uncles, grandpa, and books! There are quite a lot of lovely quotes. The best parts in the book are of course when she cuts her narrative stream of memories and speaks to Paula or about Paula. I wanted more of these instants and much less parts about flat characters and the political background in Chile. I had to skip these pages or skim through them. So what happened was that I would read a dull part about a distant relative or Salvador Allende, for example, and when I would nearly give up on the book, Isabel would write something really magical and interesting and would suck me back in. It would be cruel of me to say this should have been a 200 pages book, because I know that writing this book was a healing process and journey for the wounded mother. And for that reason, I love this book and appreciate each word in it whether it did or did not strike a chord in my heart. I will leave you with this quote:<br />"- 'Why are you crying?' you asked in an unrecognizable voice.<br />- 'Because I'm afraid. I love you, Paula.'<br />- 'I love you, too, Mama.'<br />That was the last thing you said to me, Paula."</span>
  <a data-text-id="14253626497262803902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11452831904152266269" style="display:none">Full review at <a href="http://thebibliophage.com/book-review-paula-isabel-allende/" rel="nofollow noopener">TheBibliophage.com</a><br /><br />In her wide-ranging memoir, Isabel Allende tells the story of a conversation she had with famous Chilean poet Pablo Neruda. As they talked, he said to her, “My dear child, you must be the worst journalist in the country. You are incapable of being objective, you place yourself at the center of everything you do, I suspect you’re not beyond fibbing, and when you don’t have news, you invent it. Why don’t you write novels instead? In literature, those defects are virtues.” Exactly so.<br /><br />As Allende tells her story, it’s both memoir and the history of her family. Next, layer on top some Chilean and Latin American history, and you get the picture. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2908387744" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2908387744" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143117-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571421692p2/3143117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2908387744?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3143117-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789871138852" href="/book/show/16525.Paula">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=espa%C3%B1ol">español</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=chileno">chileno</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2908387744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13163127551050868434">Isabel Allende’s novel Paula recounts the death of her daughter in 1992. Her daughter Paula had encountered the disorder Porphyria that affects the nervous system. In her case, through a variety of factors, she ended up in a coma, and after much intervention, she passed away at age 29. In short, this was not a pleasant read on the surface.<br/><br/>Twisting the tale, Allende retells her own life story to her coma-induced daughter Paula while intermingling updates along the way. The book acts on many level</span>
  <span id="freeText13163127551050868434" style="display:none">Isabel Allende’s novel Paula recounts the death of her daughter in 1992. Her daughter Paula had encountered the disorder Porphyria that affects the nervous system. In her case, through a variety of factors, she ended up in a coma, and after much intervention, she passed away at age 29. In short, this was not a pleasant read on the surface.<br /><br />Twisting the tale, Allende retells her own life story to her coma-induced daughter Paula while intermingling updates along the way. The book acts on many levels and surpasses a dark read.<br /><br />Beginning with her grandparents that inspired her first book, La casa de los espíritus, we see that magic, tarot cards and things of the other world was a family trait. Born in Peru’s to a diplomat, her father disappears after a scandal, they move back to Santiago, Chile. Her mother remarried another diplomat and the family is relocated to Lebanon in the 1950s. <br /><br />Back again to Chile after a short uprising in Lebanon, the family is reunited with her famous cousin Salvador Allende, who becomes president of Chile. Isabel gets married, has two children and begins a career as a reporter. But their time is changed again, after the American backed coup d’état. <br /><br />The family flees to Venezuela, a rich, stable country but where things take a toll on the family. Her husband is challenged with finding work, Isabel finds none, her children present issues and she flees to Spain to have an affair. Wow, this sounds like a telenovela, or fodder for a novel. After turning 40, Isabel is depressed and has no direction. When she hears that her Basque grandfather is close to death, all those ghosts in her family resurface, and her first novel is born. <br /><br />Instantly she finds fame and her life changes. Her marriage fails but she meets Willie, moving to the Bay Area around San Francisco.<br /><br />All of this surprises me but of course the main plot of the book is the story of her dying daughter. Allende has overcome tremendous challenges and now this? How does she cope? The book was published in 1994 and of course, history has shown us that Allende has become a leading novelist. Her inspiration is her family. The ghosts, the past and the present. She lays it all bare here. Perhaps this is her key. Honesty, tell it as it is, her tough upbringing by her grandparents, and unflinching love for family.<br /><br />This book was a success when it came out but reading it almost 30 years later, the historical facts were resounding. Venezuela was the place to be in Latin America (not any more). The American intervention paid off the truck drivers not to deliver food to disrupt the socialist agenda. I read this as the four Congresswomen in America where told to go back to their own countries and were played as “Socialists” revealed that not much has changed.<br /><br />The world can be a wary place. Politics disrupts lives then and now. But people, everyday people are what is at the heart of humanity. They keep us moving forward.<br /><br />A special thanks to Luis for his recent review that prompted me to read this book. It was a fascinating read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13163127551050868434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18219981?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pedro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pedro" href="/user/show/1008985-pedro">Pedro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1008985-pedro?shelf=compost-pile">compost-pile</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18219981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11741905488226868952">I was hoping this memoir would be a better read than her formulaic, run-of-the-mill, dime-store magical realist "novels" but I was disappointed. I was also hoping to learn more about her daughter, for whom the book is named. On this count, I was also disappointed. What I got instead was a formulaic, run-of-the-mill, dime-store magical realist account of her life that tilted between the kitsch and the narcissistic and that only served to further convince me of Isabel Allende's powers of self-prom</span>
  <span id="freeText11741905488226868952" style="display:none">I was hoping this memoir would be a better read than her formulaic, run-of-the-mill, dime-store magical realist "novels" but I was disappointed. I was also hoping to learn more about her daughter, for whom the book is named. On this count, I was also disappointed. What I got instead was a formulaic, run-of-the-mill, dime-store magical realist account of her life that tilted between the kitsch and the narcissistic and that only served to further convince me of Isabel Allende's powers of self-promotion. Her life is no more interesting than the life of any other member of the South American privileged classes so I'm not quite sure what all the fuss is about.<br /><br />It's sad that so much amazing Latin American literature gets overlooked because Allende and others like her keep hogging all the spotlight with their simplistic, stereotype-driven "scribblings". You can't compete against corporate marketing, I guess.<br /><br />Shameless Plug: For a real writer with a truly interesting life see Roberto Bolaño.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1703162417" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1703162417" />
    <a title="Maggi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/867546-maggi"><img alt="Maggi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203895622p2/867546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1703162417?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggi" href="/user/show/867546-maggi">Maggi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1703162417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5762613345938399997"> Written as if in a letter to a dying daughter, this gorgeously poetic and moving book tells stories of Allende's family, her own life, and even of Chile itself in language that is at times breathtaking, at others, heartbreaking. <i>You can feel the breath of the gods, throbbing, absolute presences in this resplendent domain of precipices and high walls of black rock polished by the snow to the sensual perfection of marble... This memory is sacred to me; this memory is my country. </i> <br/>We can also cred</span>
  <span id="freeText5762613345938399997" style="display:none"> Written as if in a letter to a dying daughter, this gorgeously poetic and moving book tells stories of Allende's family, her own life, and even of Chile itself in language that is at times breathtaking, at others, heartbreaking. <i>You can feel the breath of the gods, throbbing, absolute presences in this resplendent domain of precipices and high walls of black rock polished by the snow to the sensual perfection of marble... This memory is sacred to me; this memory is my country. </i> <br />We can also credit Allende's translator, Margaret Sayers Peden, for making the transition from Spanish to English work so beautifully. Allende's slow acceptance of her daughter's fate is both achingly real and spiritually uplifting. <i> I comprehend that despite everything, I am still alive because in the ferocious whirlpool, there is a merciful shaft through which I can breathe. Unresisting, I let myself be dragged down, and gradually the fear recedes. I float in an underwater cave and rest there for a while, safe from the dragons of despair.</i> <br />I don't know another author who can tell stories of the deeply soulful and also the mundane and sometimes hilarious moments of life with such true emotion. There is much to learn as well. <i>Paula </i> is as good as Allende's other memoir, <i> The Sum of Our Days, </i>which was also fabulous. More than a memoir.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5762613345938399997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152185952" />
    <a title="Aniela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4700584-aniela"><img alt="Aniela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293964716p2/4700584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152185952?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aniela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aniela" href="/user/show/4700584-aniela">Aniela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152185952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9921899126983157417">It is an autobiography written during the watching over her dying daughter. But the book is not that gloomy due to the talented combination of dramatic moments, humour and wisdom. The writer tries to find out the sense of this suffering. The power of this book is probably created by the archetype that underlies it, rendered in the classical myth of goddess Demeter descending to the Underwold in search of her daughter Persephone. The book is thus structured on 2 story lines: Isabel Allende's tumu</span>
  <span id="freeText9921899126983157417" style="display:none">It is an autobiography written during the watching over her dying daughter. But the book is not that gloomy due to the talented combination of dramatic moments, humour and wisdom. The writer tries to find out the sense of this suffering. The power of this book is probably created by the archetype that underlies it, rendered in the classical myth of goddess Demeter descending to the Underwold in search of her daughter Persephone. The book is thus structured on 2 story lines: Isabel Allende's tumultous past and the contemporary tragedy of Paula's coma. In the will fight for her daughter's life, Isabel learns to give up many egoistic excesses and she develops a deeper understanding of her own soul. But the price paid for this illumination is very heavy. Even if many topics on this book are difficult: pain, suffering, agony, death, it is still not a morbid story. Many moments liberating through their humour are scattered all over the pages. The Allende family is a spectacular one, with intriguing characters for their strangeness and their weird passions.<br /><br />Not as fascinating as Marquez, but still captivating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9921899126983157417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_201544400" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201544400" />
    <a title="Olivia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209424-olivia"><img alt="Olivia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285395195p2/4209424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201544400?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia" href="/user/show/4209424-olivia">Olivia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201544400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5068593452797210598">Beautiful in delivery, exquisite in prose. This may not be a book for everyone because of the subject. This book is written as a letter to the authors' daughter while she lays in a fatal coma. The beauty of the book is in it’s communiqué of the authors’ life as the niece of an assassinated ruler in Chile and her exile from her home country. Because I am a fan of this author and her writing style, I lunged into this memoir with the intent of understanding the author a little bit more. I am in awe</span>
  <span id="freeText5068593452797210598" style="display:none">Beautiful in delivery, exquisite in prose. This may not be a book for everyone because of the subject. This book is written as a letter to the authors' daughter while she lays in a fatal coma. The beauty of the book is in it’s communiqué of the authors’ life as the niece of an assassinated ruler in Chile and her exile from her home country. Because I am a fan of this author and her writing style, I lunged into this memoir with the intent of understanding the author a little bit more. I am in awe of Isabel Allende. The strength it would take to let your child leave the earth plane is unimaginable to me. To prepare your spirit for the death of someone so lovely; takes my breath away. Good read for those that yearn for healing on a spiritual level . . . no matter what the situation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5068593452797210598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2028353647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer226172502020374015">This is my first attempt to read Isabel Allende, and it was not a success. "Paula" got universal raves, but I just can't get into it - I feel like I've been reading it for a month and I'm only on page 30. This may be mean-spirited, and I don't mean to discount this heartbreaking and life-altering tragedy in the author's life, but it also struck me as kind of mercenary to exploit it by turning it into a novel.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_98549826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98549826" />
    <a title="Amanda B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/400386-amanda-b"><img alt="Amanda B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237932804p2/400386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98549826?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda B." href="/user/show/400386-amanda-b">Amanda B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/400386-amanda-b?shelf=advisorybooks-2009-10">advisorybooks-2009-10</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98549826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9824952962091067200">I have become very interested in Isabel Allende’s books. She is a very impressive author and the facts that she integrates her Hispanic culture makes me eager to read her books. This particular book came to my attention from my older sister’s book stash. I have read The House of the Spirits which contained elements of magical realism, and the moment I saw that this was a memoir I wanted to read it all the more. I was interested to see how this one author could write in these two different genres</span>
  <span id="freeText9824952962091067200" style="display:none">I have become very interested in Isabel Allende’s books. She is a very impressive author and the facts that she integrates her Hispanic culture makes me eager to read her books. This particular book came to my attention from my older sister’s book stash. I have read The House of the Spirits which contained elements of magical realism, and the moment I saw that this was a memoir I wanted to read it all the more. I was interested to see how this one author could write in these two different genres. A novel has components of fiction, but a memoir has far more non fiction which makes any story more interesting. <br /><br />Although I had a lot of excitement and little hesitation, the premise of this memoir was very emotional. Allende tells the story of her daughter Paula, and how she fell into a coma after getting ill. The whole memoir is about what Allende was telling, and writing, her daughter during this time. Allende would occupy her time in telling Paula stories of their family, in hopes that she would gain strength from them. This story is so captivating because it is depicts a beautiful relationship between a mother and her daughter. Allende fought for her daughter until the end believing that she would be ok, when in fact things did not go as planned. The emotions Allende felt were emitting off of the pages and I truly felt for her. The ways in which she hopefully told each story and constantly spoke to her daughter seemed so kind and pure which drew me into reading more. This is one of the most beautiful books I have read, because her motherly love is evident and I could feel what she felt. I have had a couple people pass away in my family, but I have never been there as it was happening. I was only allowed to go to the funerals; but in reading this book, I could understand what the families of the now deceased had to go through. I would undoubtedly read this book again, as well as recommend it to others. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9824952962091067200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h9aL2Dso+PzBoX0Wv7ZjXaPVZ6gC6nkL7gROs80acO6aP2hR1UcjP1LuLdi+F6ZWqFvptcdffNs4PyCY5jf+xg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Apenas unos meses han pasado desde que el joven Alexander Cold siguio a su audaz abuela al corazon del Amazonas para descubrir su bestia legendaria. En esta ocasion, la reportera Kate Cold acompana a su nieto y a su mejor amiga, Nadia, junto con los fotografos de International Geographic, a hacer un viaje a otro lugar remoto del mundo. En un vedado estado independiente enclavado entre las cumbres heladas de los Himalayas, la tarea del equipo consiste en localizar a su legendario Dragon de Oro, una estatua sagrada y un oraculo invaluable que puede predecir el futuro del reino. En su lucha para llegar a la estatua antes de que sea destruida por la avaricia de un intruso, Alexander y Nadia deben usar el poder trascendente de los espiritus de animales totemicos, Jaguar y Aguila. But Tita falls in love with Pedro, and he is seduced by the magical food she cooks. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2545614799483279296">Isabel Allende Llona is a Chilean-American novelist. Allende, who writes in the "magic realism" tradition, is considered one of the first successful women novelists in Latin America. She has written novels based in part on her own experiences, often focusing on the experiences of women, weaving myth and realism together. She has lectured and done extensive book tours and has taught literature at s</span>
  <span id="freeText2545614799483279296" style="display:none">Isabel Allende Llona is a Chilean-American novelist. Allende, who writes in the "magic realism" tradition, is considered one of the first successful women novelists in Latin America. She has written novels based in part on her own experiences, often focusing on the experiences of women, weaving myth and realism together. She has lectured and done extensive book tours and has taught literature at several US colleges. She currently resides in California with her husband. Allende adopted U.S. citizenship in 2003.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2545614799483279296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
